Mayor Zhang Adopts the Tax Reduction Opinions of the Shanghai Municipal Business Reorganization Council

The Shanghai Special Municipality Business Reorganization Council previously sent a letter to Mayor Zhang regarding the issue of donation taxes in the city, expressing opinions in order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. Mayor Zhang agreed to adopt the opinions, and the Business Reorganization Council sent a reply to express gratitude. The original correspondence is recorded below:

Mayor's Letter to the Business Reorganization Council: In response, I have carefully read your letter and am well aware of your opinions. It demonstrates your council's concern for municipal affairs and consideration for the people's hardships, which is deeply admirable. Your letter earnestly advocates for the abolition of harsh and miscellaneous taxes. This can indeed serve as a guideline for financial management and is also what the municipal government adheres to as a principle. The current tax system in Shanghai mostly follows the old regulations of the former Shanghai North Industrial and Patrol Donation Bureau and the Nanshi Municipal Office. Since the situation is different now than in the past, there should be room for deliberation and improvement. In July 1928, a resolution was passed at the municipal affairs meeting to establish a Finance Committee to discuss the nature and collection procedures of various donation taxes. Subsequently, a general outline for reorganization was drafted, with the aim of abolishing harsh and minor taxes, which coincides with the advocacy of your council. Therefore, whenever a tax system is formulated, it is always examined to see if it conforms to this principle in order to determine whether to adopt or reject it. Furthermore, since it concerns increasing the burden on citizens, opinions from all parties must be gathered in order to make a decision. The finalized cases are on record and can be verified. Now, I will try to explain the process of the various donation taxes mentioned in your letter to your council in general terms. (1) Cattle and Sheep Inspection Fees: Originally, the city only had a pig slaughter tax, which was collected by the Shanghai County Office. After the establishment of the city, in order to ensure public food hygiene, regulations for slaughtering and inspection of livestock were formulated, first for the pig industry and then for the cattle and sheep industry. Since various technical drugs are required during the inspection, it is necessary to charge fees to cover the costs. For cattle and sheep transported to the concession, pre-slaughter inspection is implemented, the purpose of which is to protect the health of Chinese citizens in the concession. Its nature is a handling fee, not a donation tax. The Finance Bureau convened a meeting with all parties, and your council sent representatives to attend the discussion before the final decision was made. If inspecting and slaughtering livestock is deemed a necessary task, then charging fees is a natural result. If there are any aspects of the fee collection procedure that are deemed unsatisfactory, then the method is not immutable and can be improved. (2) Ship Donation Tax: The city's ship donation tax was originally a type of special donation for public welfare during the Qing Dynasty's self-government office era. After the establishment of the city, it was reorganized for the sake of unified collection. In August of last year, the ship donation tax regulations were revised again. In order to regulate ships, the Public Utilities Bureau drafted regulations for inspecting ships and ship license regulations, which were submitted for promulgation. Shipowners complained that the donation rate was too high, causing disputes. The Finance Bureau invited all parties concerned to meet at your council to jointly study the matter. However, since the sixth and seventh classes were relatively high, they were reduced separately. However, the shipowners still held different opinions. After further discussion by the government, it was determined that inspection was crucial to water safety and could not be suspended, while the donation rate could be reduced. Subsequently, it was decided that the donation rates for the first, second, third, and fourth classes would remain the same, the fifth class would be reduced to 2.75 yuan, the sixth class would be reduced to 3.57 yuan, and the seventh class would be reduced to 4.22 yuan. The license fee was reduced to 3 yuan. All registration procedures will still be handled in accordance with the methods agreed upon by all parties at your council on that day, with simplicity and speed as the main principles. All shipowners who pay taxes at the original donation rate should be reimbursed based on the receipt to demonstrate fairness, and this has been notified by the city in a separate case. (3) Banquet Donation Tax: The establishment of the city's banquet donation tax originally came from the construction of merchants. According to the Finance Bureau's report, Dafugui Restaurant and others jointly submitted a petition stating that banquet donation taxes had been established in the capitals of Hangzhou and Guangzhou for a long time. The Shanghai urban area is prosperous, and there are many banquets. It is proposed to imitate them. After detailed discussion by the bureau, it was deemed feasible. The proposed donation rate is 5% for each banquet worth more than 3 yuan. This donation tax is levied on diners, not on shops, so its nature is a consumption tax. Your letter mistakenly considers it to be a business tax. This donation tax has been implemented in other provinces, and it is appropriate to imitate it in order to increase the city's revenue. However, whether it has a significant impact on the business of shops should be considered. Since you have given instructions, it should be reconsidered in order to be most appropriate. (4) Incense, Candles, and Firecrackers Business Tax: The Finance Bureau is responsible for taxation throughout the city and can investigate the status of various businesses at any time. This tax item has not been implemented in the city. Your letter is a misunderstanding. Most of the above donation taxes that have been implemented have been discussed with the participation of your council. All instructions have been implemented. It is the city government's consideration of commercial conditions, with absolutely no prejudice. This can be understood by your council. Furthermore, the city has only been established for three years, and various undertakings are expanding day by day. Municipal administration cannot be carried out without funds. The way to increase the city's revenue is nothing more than expanding sources and reducing expenditures. But in terms of expanding sources, the local government cannot rely mainly on tax revenue. If what is levied fully complies with the principles of taxation, then it cannot be said to be harming the people. The increase in the burden on the people is unavoidable in the construction process. The balance between the consequences of sacrificing enjoyment and the benefits and obligations depends on a long-term vision, and planning should be long-term. You are all intelligent and should have insight into this. However, the situation in the city is special. On the one hand, the concessions have not yet been recovered. On the other hand, although the administrative powers of the province and city have been divided, the Jiangsu provincial tax collection agencies are still located in the city, resulting in disparate tax systems and increased burdens. Therefore, it is not easy to comply with the principles of fairness and universality, no matter what tax is implemented. This is why the city government is so careful in considering things repeatedly. Regarding the wharf donation, it is currently in progress and has just begun. It can live up to your expectations and recover lost rights. In terms of reducing expenditures, the city's budget increases year by year due to the expansion of operations. The allocation of its expenditures follows a certain standard. The city is made up of the people, and the government is established by the people. All measures are aimed at increasing the welfare of the citizens. Therefore, what is taken from the people

Page 14

should be used for the people. This is what the city government dares to sincerely tell you. As for the various bureaus and personnel used by the city government, they are all based on the special city organization law promulgated by the central government. There are no additional agencies, and the annual budget makes every effort to save on administrative expenses. At this time when the revolution has not yet succeeded, those who serve the city should have the spirit of hard work and struggle. For the sake of their own welfare, citizens should have a willingness to cooperate in the implementation of municipal facilities. Your council leads the people and knows the people's feelings. Your earnest instructions are of great benefit to the city. I am sending this brief reply in the hope that you will give it your attention. Sincerely, Zhang Qun.

Reply from the Business Reorganization Council to the Mayor: To Mayor, with respect and humility, I previously ventured to comment on the city's tax affairs because I witnessed the people's strength declining and heard the masses' appeals every day. I was afraid that my words were激切 and would offend your dignity. However, I received a reply with earnest encouragement, stating that the city's situation is special, the tax system is disparate, and the burden is increased. It is difficult to comply with the principles of fairness and universality, no matter what tax is implemented, which demonstrates your concern for the people's hardships at all times. Your humility and sincerity are comparable to those of former sages. I look up to you from below with endless admiration. Later, I received two clear orders, for the ship donation tax, to reduce the amount according to class, and for the banquet donation tax, to approve the immediate suspension of implementation, which further demonstrates the reality of taking advice as a way to improve, rather than merely comforting with warm words. After hearing the order, I was deeply moved and admired. However, no matter what tax is implemented in the city, since the situation is special and it is difficult to comply with the principles of fairness and universality, it is more difficult to promote it to the fullest extent and reduce harassment than in other cities. It seems that extra care should be taken. Rather than waiting for the donation rate to be announced and implemented, and then changing it in response to the people's requests, the procedures are difficult, and the time may be delayed. Although your kindness is conveyed, the merchants and people will inevitably suffer losses first. The matter of the ship donation tax is one example. It is better to take the opportunity when the policy has not yet been decided to first convene the relevant businesses to consult as much as possible, and then announce and implement it after the method is satisfactory and there are no obstacles. This is easier for both officials and merchants. This is the humble opinion of adopting it before the event rather than making improvements after the event. If you consider this simple view to be acceptable, I propose that in the future, all matters relating to the revision of tax regulations should first convene the relevant businesses to give them the opportunity to present the advantages and disadvantages and make as many contributions as possible, so that there will be less obstacles in advance and to highlight the goodness of making orders effective. Whether this is appropriate or not, I hope you will review and instruct us to comply.

The Municipal Government Announces the Articles of Association of the Municipal Bank

The Shanghai Municipal Bank Will Open on the 17th of This Month. The Articles of Association of the Bank Have Also Been Announced by the Municipal Government. A Special Excerpt Is As Follows: Chapter 1: General Provisions Article 1: This bank is designated as the Shanghai Special Municipality Municipal Bank and is named the Shanghai Municipal Bank. It shall be approved and registered by the Ministry of Finance upon consultation with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. Article 2: This bank shall be located in the central district of the Shanghai Special Municipality. Branches or offices may be established in important locations in the city, which shall be filed with the Ministry of Finance upon consultation with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. However, before the central district is developed, the head office may be temporarily located in a prosperous area of the city. Article 3: The bank's operating period is 30 years. Upon expiration, it may be extended upon approval by the Ministry of Finance after consultation with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. Chapter 2: Capital Article 4: The total capital of the bank is set at 1 million yuan in national currency, which shall be fully allocated by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government in one lump sum to start business. When it is necessary to increase capital or attract commercial shares due to business needs, it shall be approved by the Ministry of Finance after a resolution by the Board of Directors upon consultation with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. Chapter 3: Business Article 5: The bank's business is as follows: (1) Mortgage loans and discounted bills for industrial and commercial enterprises in the city; (2) Management of national, local, or corporate bonds; (3) Various deposits; (4) Trading of securities; (5) Other banking businesses approved by the Board of Directors. Article 6: The bank may manage the following businesses entrusted by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government: (1) Acting as an agent for the issuance of bonds by the municipal government and the repayment of principal and interest; (2) Custody of the property and funds of municipal agencies or public organizations; (3) Handling loan matters for the poor. Chapter 4: Organization Article 7: The bank shall have five directors and three supervisors, who shall be appointed by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. However, two directors and one supervisor shall be selected from the financial community in the city. The term of office for directors is three years, and the term of office for supervisors is one year. They may be reappointed. After the appointment of the aforementioned directors and supervisors, they shall be filed with the Ministry of Finance upon consultation with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government. Article 8: The bank shall have one general manager, who shall be appointed by the mayor from among the directors. One manager and one or two deputy managers shall be appointed by the general manager with the approval of the Board of Directors and reported to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for record. Article 9: The general manager shall be responsible for all affairs of the bank internally and represent the bank externally. The manager shall assist the general manager and the deputy manager in handling all bank affairs. Chapter 5: Board of Directors Article 10: The powers of the Board of Directors are as follows: (1) Compilation of various rules and regulations; (2) Determination of business policies; (3) Establishment or revocation of branches or offices; (4) Review of various external contracts; (5) Approval of various expenditures; (6) Review and approval of budgets and final accounts. Article 11: The general manager shall serve as the chairman when the Board of Directors meets. In the event of an accident, the general manager may entrust another director to act as his agent. Article 12: A meeting of the Board of Directors shall be held with the attendance of more than half of the directors. A resolution may be adopted with the consent of more than half of the directors present. When the number of votes for and against is equal, the chairman shall make the final decision. Article 13: If a director is unable to attend due to an event, he may entrust another director as his representative. Article 14: The minutes of the Board of Directors meeting shall be signed or sealed by the chairman and preserved. Chapter 6: Board of Supervisors Article 15: The powers of the Board of Supervisors are as follows: (1) Reviewing the business and property conditions and presenting opinions to the Board of Directors when necessary; (2) Reviewing all accounts and final accounts reports; (3) Supervising whether employees comply with all regulations, articles of association, and resolutions of the Board of Directors in performing their duties. Chapter 7: Final Accounts Article 16: June of each year is the semi-annual final account period, and December is the annual total final account period. The following tables and booklets shall be prepared and submitted to the Board of Directors for reporting to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for review by the Ministry of Finance: (1) Inventory of property; (2) Balance sheet; (3) Business report; (4) Profit and loss statement; (5) Surplus distribution statement. Article 17: The bank shall set aside at least 30% of the annual net profit as a public reserve fund, and the remainder shall be decided by the Board of Directors and reported to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for record. Chapter 8: Supplementary Provisions Article 18: If there are any matters not covered in these Articles of Association, they shall be resolved by the Board of Directors and reported to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for approval and amendment by the Ministry of Finance. Article 19: These Articles of Association shall be implemented from the date of approval.

Inspection Report of the Central Bank

Forty-Fourth Time

The Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank in this city held its forty-fourth inspection on February 10 at the bank's Issuing Bureau. The results are announced as follows: The total amount of exchange coupons issued is 14,120,284 yuan, including 12,654,522 yuan in silver yuan coupons and 1,465,762 yuan in auxiliary currency coupons equivalent to silver dollars. The total amount of exchange coupon reserves is 14,120,284 yuan, including 9,277,279.20 yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves include 5,500,936.82 yuan in the bank's issuing vault, 1,130,835.14 yuan in branches in various cities, and 2,628,107.24 yuan in the same industry. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 4,842,004.80 yuan in silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Exchange Coupon Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. February 10, 1930, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fusun, Supervisors Wang Yihou, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Zhiqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilu.

Four Banks Preparation Vault Issuance Preparation Report

Sixth Time

The Four Banks Preparation Vault is jointly established by the Y盐业, Jincheng 金城, Zhongnan 中南, and Continental 大陆 four banks, specializing in the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the vault's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with 100% reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for at most 40%. It is announced once a week and audited by the four banks' auditors and accountants. The total amount of reserves is 23,427,113 yuan, including 14,497,329.86 yuan in cash reserves and 8,929,783.14 yuan in guarantee reserves.

The Bureau of Commodity Inspection Prepares for the Inspection of Lace

Merchants from lace factories in this city and other cities previously stated that lace is a special handicraft product of China. However, in recent years, lace merchants have not been diligent in improving the style, quality, and materials of their goods, resulting in a decline in the industry and affecting international credit. It is imperative to remedy this situation. They jointly submitted a petition to the Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting attention to rectification and unified inspection in order to promote development. After receiving the petition, the bureau considered that the manufacturers are paying attention to developing overseas trade and voluntarily requesting the inspection of lace, which is commendable. It immediately approved the petition and prepared to set up an office for inspection. It requested the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to appoint Ms. Chen Jinduan as a technician and acting director, and Tao Yumen as deputy director, to actively carry out the work. Ms. Chen graduated from the Boston School of Fine Arts in the United States and studied fine arts in Paris. She has served as an art teacher at the Shanghai Chinese and Western Girls' School. Mr. Tao has been engaged in the lace business for more than ten years and has rich experience. They are currently drafting manufacturing standards for lace, drafting detailed inspection rules, and soliciting opinions from merchants. They are scheduled to send the patterns to the bureau by the 20th of this month so that they can gather wisdom and register them separately. Once the facilities are completed, inspection will be implemented on a scheduled basis.

The Inspection of Raw Silk Is Postponed for One Month

Implementation on March 1

Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in order to develop the European sales of Chinese silk, specially ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to set up a Raw Silk Inspection Office and scheduled to start inspecting exported raw silk on the 1st of this month. Subsequently, the Chinese silk merchants requested a postponement. Director Zou submitted a request to Minister Kong, who approved the postponement for one month, scheduling the implementation on March 1. Director Zou has notified the factory owners and silk merchants of the Yellow, White, and Gray grades.

Standard for Calculating Road Construction Fees in This City

No Fees Levied on Expropriated Land

The road construction fees in this city, previously stipulated by the Municipal Bureau of Public Works in a temporary ordinance, separately specified the percentage of road construction fees. However, the standard for calculating this percentage, whether it should be based on the original area before expropriation or the remaining area after expropriation, was not clearly defined, causing difficulties for the Bureau in handling this matter. Recently, a request was submitted to the Municipal Government to approve that the calculation standard for this item should be based on the remaining beneficial area for fair assessment and collection. The Municipal Government considered that the purpose of collecting road construction fees is that although the land has been expropriated, the value of the un-expropriated land has increased sharply due to road construction. Therefore, collecting fees is based on the mutual establishment of rights and obligations. If the land has already been expropriated, and it is still required to pay fees in accordance with the ordinance, it would be unfair to make people lose land and have to pay taxes. The Bureau has been instructed to exclude the expropriated land and only collect fees based on the percentage calculated from the remaining beneficial land.

Temporary Rules for Tenant Farmers Paying Rent in This City

Announced by the Municipal Government

The Municipal Land and Social Bureaus have recently drafted sixteen temporary rules for tenant farmers paying rent in this city, referring to the tenant farmer rent payment regulations of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and considering the customary rent payment practices of landlords and tenants in various rural areas of this city, as well as the Shatin landlord and tenant rent payment methods. These rules have been submitted to and approved by the Municipal Government for implementation. The original text of the rules is recorded as follows: Article 1: These temporary rules apply to all relationships of rent payment or subletting between tenant farmers within the special municipality. Article 2: The percentage of rent payment and subletting shall be based on the following limits: (1) Rent payment: The maximum limit shall not exceed 35% of the total local average normal yield; (2) Subletting: The landlord shall receive 35% of the total normal yield, and the tenant shall receive 65% of the total normal yield. Article 3: If the rent exceeds the limits stipulated in the preceding article, it shall be reduced immediately. If it does not exceed the limits, it shall remain as before. Article 4: If a tenant owes rent before the implementation of these temporary rules, and the repayment is after the implementation, it shall be paid according to the original practice. Article 5: All small rent levies, miscellaneous fees, and all kinds of malpractices are prohibited. Article 6: If there are subsidiary mulberry trees, bamboo, fruit trees, reeds, ponds, etc. attached to the land, which can generate annual income, no additional rent shall be levied unless otherwise stipulated. Article 7: The time and location of rent payment shall still be determined according to local customs. Article 8: All contracts with advance rent provisions are invalid. Article 9: Rent payment is limited to the local produce of the current year. If there is an agreement between the tenants to pay rent in cash, the amount of cash shall be equivalent to the price of the produce to be paid. The price shall be based on the highest, lowest, and average local market prices at the time of payment as agreed. Article 10: Rent payment shall be based on national standard weights and measures. However, before the general use of weights and measures in the area, it shall be compared and converted. Article 11: In the event of a poor harvest due to natural disasters, pests, or other force majeure events, the amount of rent payment shall be determined proportionally according to the degree of poor harvest. Article 12: Tenants who do not abandon planting and pay rent on time according to the rent amount shall not be evicted without reason, but special agreements shall be followed. Article 13: Landlords shall issue receipts or other similar proofs when receiving rent. Article 14: If a tenant does not pay rent in accordance with these rules, and the amount of rent owed is full for two years, the landlord may evict the tenant and re-rent the land. Article 15: In the event of disputes arising from rent payment or subletting, the Social Bureau may be petitioned for handling. Article 16: These temporary rules shall be implemented from the date of announcement by the Special Municipal Government.

Railway Bureau's Plan to Facilitate Passengers

Contract Signed with Three Automobile Companies

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, in order to facilitate passengers on both routes, has signed a passenger car contract with the Linji Yongxing North Station Three Automobile Companies. The fare schedule is listed as follows: 65 cents per trip, with 20 minutes as the base. Trips under 20 minutes will also be calculated as 20 minutes. Beyond 20 minutes, each additional 5 minutes will cost 17 cents. The first hour costs 2 yuan, and the second and third hours cost 1.5 yuan per hour. Any odd minutes beyond the full hour will be calculated as a minimum of 20 minutes. Over 40 minutes will be counted as one hour. Beyond four hours, each hour will cost 1 yuan. Over 20 minutes will be counted as one hour. Twelve hours to sixteen hours cost 14 yuan. From 7:00 AM to 11:00 PM, it is considered a full day. It is also stipulated that trips from the North Station to the following locations will cost 1 yuan each: Shanghai University, Guanghua University, Gaochang Temple, Longhua, Zhoujiaqiao, Zhenru, Caohejing, Fanwangdu, Yangshupu Bottom, Caojiadu, etc.

Recent News in the Shipping Industry

More Cargo, Fewer Ships on the Yangtze River - A considerable amount of Yangtze River cargo accumulated in Shanghai last winter has not yet been shipped. Now that the river is gradually rising, loading is being rushed. However, only four Chinese ships are available for departure these days. Many passengers and goods that cannot be loaded are being taken by foreign ships. The China Merchants Bureau has already transferred the Hai Lun Yu Shun to the Yangtze River to barely maintain commercial transportation. Yesterday, the Sanbei Company also leased the Xin Baohua wheel from the Ping An Company at a monthly rent of 4,000 yuan, with a temporary lease term of two and a half months, and also dispatched it to Shanghai and Hankou to meet passenger demand. However, the ship is relatively small and can only carry 600 tons, which is slightly better than nothing.

Longhai Locomotives Arrive in Shanghai - The Longhai Railway, in order to reorganize passenger cars, has purchased a batch of new locomotives from Belgium. The first batch consists of four locomotives, each weighing over 22 tons and being the latest model. Originally, they were planned to be unloaded in Pukou and transferred to Henan. However, fearing obstacles, it has been decided that when the locomotives are imported on the 15th, they will be temporarily stored in Shanghai and a way will be found to transport them later.

Continued News on the Pacific Shipping Turmoil

The Pacific shipping turmoil caused by Japanese ship competition has been reported in this newspaper. The current competition and remedies of each wheel company will be further reported as follows:

Striving for Silk Loading - This turmoil started with the competition for transporting Huzhou silk. According to statistics, a total of 557,000 bales of Chinese silk were shipped to the United States last year. Based on the original price, the freight would require more than 8.8 million yuan in Chinese currency. Since the gold price increase, the amount of Chinese silk going to the United States has increased because American merchants who handle Japanese silk have switched to purchasing Chinese silk. Therefore, this year's silk export volume should be higher than last year. Since Japanese merchants have reduced freight rates, the annual freight income for silk shipped to the United States will be reduced by 7 million yuan. During this period of drastic freight rate cuts, various companies are competing fiercely for transportation. The Gorret Wheel of Xiangtai Foreign Company is carrying a full load of Huzhou silk for export to the United States this time. In the past, the freight rates for silk on Sino-American wheels were the most favorable, but now they have changed to the worst freight rates.

Discussing Price Reductions - Commercial wheels traveling the Shanghai-New York route have been competing fiercely with Pacific wheels in transportation since the change to express ships last year, and they also load a lot of Huzhou silk. The reduction is 5.5 US dollars per 100 pounds. It is found that companies joining this route include the Papohui William Sun Company, jointly run by Norway and the United States, the Dankel Wensheng Company, British Prince, Bank, Fort, American Standard, Ocean, and other wheel companies. Currently, each of these companies is still discussing the matter of reducing the silk transportation price to four yuan per 100 pounds, but it must be realized. Another discussion is to improve loading and transportation methods, but it has not yet been announced.

Remedying the Disturbance - Since the Japanese merchants lowered prices twice, various foreign wheel companies have recognized that if this continues, the wheel industry between China and the United States will face extreme danger. However, according to general observations, the Japanese are already implementing disturbances and have support to rely on. It is possible that they will further lower the prices. It is also heard that various wheel companies in the Pacific recognize that this chaotic price reduction by Japanese merchants is business competition, which is not in line with commercial regulations and loses the righteousness of commercial warfare. The companies have discussed many times and plan to have the various shipping companies in the association persuade the non-member Japanese merchants such as Kawasaki Mitsui to join the Pacific Water Foot Association to prevent them from causing further disturbances. However, the Japanese have other ideas, and persuasion may not be effective.

Swiftness of European Mail

Arrival in 18 Days Possible

The Shanghai Times reports that recently, mail from Europe to Shanghai via Siberia has become increasingly swift. Letters sent on January 23 can arrive in Shanghai on February 10, taking only 18 days. London newspapers published on January 24 were already in the hands of local postmen yesterday (11th), also taking only 18 days. It can be said that it has restored the old view of the fastest time of the year. Previously, mail via Siberia was privately opened three times en route, but it has not been seen again recently. However, these three cases of private opening are still being investigated by the postal authorities in London and this port, and there are still no results.

Announcement from the Pharmaceutical Association to Vigorously Promote the National Calendar

Eliminate Discounts on the Lunar Calendar and Issue Wages According to the National Calendar

The Pharmaceutical Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' Association for the Promotion of National Products, in order to comply with the National Calendar and eliminate old practices, decided at a joint meeting of the Executive Discipline Committee yesterday to eliminate discounts on the lunar calendar and correct the issuance of wages to employees according to the National Calendar, and abolish all malpractices of the lunar calendar. The announcement to the industry in the city is as follows: In the matter of announcement, it has been repeatedly ordered by the central government to abolish the lunar calendar and vigorously promote the National Calendar, which should be strictly followed. However, in the old practices of our industry, there have been discounts on the first and fifteenth days of the lunar calendar and the first and fifteenth days of the solar calendar. Now that the lunar calendar has been abolished and the National Calendar is followed, there is no lunar or solar calendar, so it is essential to eliminate old practices. Therefore, the Executive Discipline Committee of this association has decided that from this year, all old practices of the lunar calendar in our industry will be eliminated, and only discounts on the first and fifteenth days of the National Calendar will be allowed. Those who violate this decision and continue the old practices will be severely punished. This decision, in addition to being submitted by this association to the Social Bureau for approval and execution, must be strictly followed by all of our colleagues. As for the elimination of old practices, the procedures are complicated, which this association is well aware of. The Secretariat is rushing to draft implementation measures to facilitate compliance. As soon as the procedures are complete, they will be implemented on a regular basis. Furthermore, the issuance of wages to employees in our industry has always followed the lunar calendar. Now, it will also be corrected and wages will be paid according to the National Calendar. However, the date of wage payment may be determined by the employer. All other malpractices related to the abolition of the lunar calendar and holidays will be fundamentally eliminated from this year onwards and must not be privately implemented in violation of the order. Use the spirit of party governance to emphasize the national government's orders. This is an important announcement.

Shanghai County Magistrate Leng Changed to Acting

Leng Jun, the acting magistrate of Shanghai County, has worked hard on political work since taking office last year. Now, he has been ordered by the provincial government to change to acting, in order to encourage him. The county magistrate has been instructed by the Department of Civil Affairs to be informed.

Change of Head of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau

Vacancy Filled by Shen Jinghua Appointed by the Department of Civil Affairs

The Shanghai County Government received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs yesterday, stating that Zhu Chang, the head of the County Public Security Bureau, has been transferred to the province and is awaiting further appointment. The vacancy has been filled by Shen Jinghua, the head of the Rugao County Public Security Bureau. After Shen arrives, he will immediately hand over the work and report the situation. Therefore, Magistrate Leng has ordered Director Zhu to handle the closing matters in order to facilitate the handover. It is heard that Shen has come to Shanghai after receiving the order. After visiting Magistrate Leng at the County Government at 10:00 AM yesterday, he went to the County Public Security Bureau to visit Director Zhu, had a conversation, and then left. He will take over the work at the bureau soon.

Health Bureau Pays Attention to Epidemics in Neighboring Areas

The Municipal Health Bureau, seeing reports that meningitis is prevalent in Xinzhuang Town and nearby villages, is deeply concerned that it may affect the city. It has sent doctors from the Epidemic Prevention Section of the Fourth Department to investigate. According to the district chief and patrol officers, many people have died recently due to illness. The reported symptoms are similar to meningitis, but it is difficult to confirm without examining patients. However, for the sake of careful prevention, the doctor sent by the Health Bureau distributed leaflets in the town with meningitis prevention knowledge and practical methods for handling infectious diseases in the family, and asked the town's district chief to reprint and widely distribute them to prevent the spread of the disease. In addition, a public lecture was held in the town's teahouse on the dangers of epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis, its symptoms, transmission routes, prevention, and treatment methods. Many people listened. The notice issued by the bureau is summarized as follows: (Main symptoms of epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis) High fever, headache, pain in the waist and limbs, extreme sensitivity, stiffness in various parts of the body, generalized backward arching, or sunken abdomen, locked jaw, coma, and delirium. (Prevention and treatment methods) Do not get close to patients, do not go to places where many people gather. Those who are sick should go to the hospital for treatment and be isolated. Patients' clothes and utensils should be disinfected, that is, boiled in boiling water, or soaked in lime water for three days before being reused. The sick room should be disinfected with sulfur formalin and other disinfectant vapor. It is also heard that the Municipal Health Bureau can provide formalin disinfectors for the convenience of sick families, each large size costing two yuan and each small size costing one yuan and sixty cents.

Sino-Japanese Trade Gradually Declines

Complex Reasons

Guowen News Agency reports that in January, Japan's total exports were 145 million yen, a decrease from the previous period. Among them, the total value of exports to China was 31 million yen, with exports exceeding 9 million yuan. Compared with the same period last year, it decreased by more than 12 million yuan. Sino-Japanese trade is deteriorating, and the reasons are extremely complex.
