Local News Two

The Provisional Court Yesterday Heard the Case of a Woman Conspiring to Kill Her Stepmother

The Courtroom Was Filled with Spectators

The Small Knife Belonged to Zhang Wenqing

The Bloody Handprint on the Back Door

The Judge Instructed the Police to Investigate

Yesterday afternoon at 2:30, Judge Luo Renji, accompanied by Mr. Menghatt, the American consul acting as a trial observer, took the bench in the First Tribunal of the Provisional Court to hear the case of Zhang Wenqing, a woman who, in order to compete for inheritance, conspired with Chen Hengcai, Yao Yonggui, Gao Jintang, etc. to kill her stepmother. When the case was opened, there were many relatives and friends of both parties and staff members of the court present in the courtroom, which was full of people. The details of the case and the opening of the trial are detailed below:

The Story of the Case - There was a man named Zhang Fusheng from Huzhou, who served as a magistrate in Zhili during the Qing Dynasty. He had some savings. After resigning, he moved his family to Shanghai and lived at No. 762 Card Road, Xinzha. Zhang had one wife and one concubine. The wife, surnamed Su, had two daughters, the eldest, Wenqing, who is now 24 years old and not yet married, and the younger, who is married. The concubine, also surnamed Su, is 34 years old and has two sons, the eldest, Jinbao, whose style name is Wenjin, is thirteen years old, and the youngest, Qianbao, whose style name is Wenqian, is eleven years old. The wife and concubine lived together. Later, Fusheng died of illness, and disputes arose between the wife and concubine over the inheritance. Because Fusheng had several thousand taels of cash during his lifetime, deposited in the Siming Xingye Bank in Shanghai, the deposit book fell into the hands of the concubine, who refused to hand it over. Therefore, Wenqing, the eldest daughter of the wife, reported the loss to the bank. The concubine then filed a criminal complaint against her major wife in the Provisional Court. Although she was summoned, the case was eventually dismissed due to reconciliation between the two parties. Later, the major wife also filed a civil lawsuit against the concubine. As a result, at the time of reconciliation, Zhang Su suddenly died. The police detectives Lang Jin and Bao Tan Yu Changyuan from Gordon Road, who were in charge of the case, arrested the suspects Zhang Wenqing and Chen Hengcai. They confessed that the murderers Yao Yonggui and Gao Jintang were hiding in Zhenjiang. The detectives went to Zhenjiang and arrested Yao and Gao and brought them back to the police station. They were sent to the Provisional Court for interrogation. The details have been reported in this newspaper.

Need to Ask the Eldest Daughter - The hearing continued yesterday. The family of the deceased hired two lawyers, Wang Xiangugu and others, while the defendant, Zhang Wenqing, hired three lawyers, Wang Fushang, Jiang Baoli, and Jiang Baolian, to defend her. First, the police lawyer Ru Bao-yi presented the case. Then, the witness Cai Hou-an testified that he was a pharmacist at the Red Cross Society on Xinzha Road. On the afternoon of the 25th of last month, at 6:00 PM, the injured Zhang Su was sent by Zhang Wenqing and a neighboring woman by rickshaw. According to Wenqing, she was stabbed by a thief at home. He saw that the injured had knife wounds on her head and hands. He and Gu Shiliang helped bandage the wounds. He asked the injured about the reason, who said that the eldest daughter (i.e., Wenqing) knew about it. He also saw Wenqing unbutton the injured's clothes and take away a piece of paper. After a quarter of an hour, the Chinese and Western detectives from the police station arrived and questioned the injured. He only heard the injured say that asking the eldest daughter would know about it. Gu Shiliang also testified that he was a nurse at the Red Cross Society. He only heard Zhang Wenqing ask the injured about the murderer. Before leaving, he said, "Not only will I stab you (i.e., the injured) to death, but I will also kill your two sons and me." The injured did not speak. Later, the police detective Bao arrived and asked the injured about the reason for being stabbed and whether there was any illicit relationship. The injured replied that she needed to ask the eldest daughter.

Tricked into the Parlor - Yu Changyuan, the police detective, testified that he and the Western detective chief Mike Wailen went to the Red Cross Society at 7:00 PM that night to question the injured. According to her, Chen Hengcai knew the eldest young lady Wenqing. At that time, Hengcai's aunt's brother Yonggui brought an unknown person. They tricked her into the parlor, and the unknown person suddenly stabbed her with a knife.

Testimony of the Eldest and Youngest Sons - Zhang Jinbao, the eldest son of the deceased, testified that he was thirteen years old. He called Wenqing "eldest sister." When his mother was attacked, he was out playing. At 6:00 PM, he and his younger brother returned home and entered through the back door. Yao Yonggui opened the door, and Yao immediately ran away with an unknown person. He went to the back patio and saw his eldest sister running down from upstairs and saw his mother lying on the ground. When his mother saw his brothers, she called his name several times and told him to go to his maternal uncle's place. The unknown person was the fourth defendant, Gao Jintang. The younger son, Zhang Qianbao, also testified.

Held the Knife and Stabbed to Death - Yao Yonggui, the defendant, testified that he was from Zhenjiang and lived at No. 751 Kangnao Road in Shanghai, where he opened a tiger stove. Chen Hengcai was a relative of his. He did not often go to the Zhang family's house. On that day, Hengcai came and asked him to fight at Card Road. He went to Zhang's house with Gao Jintang. The door was wide open. He entered. There was no one else downstairs. He talked to the deceased. Not long after, Gao held a knife and stabbed the deceased violently. At that time, the eldest and youngest ladies were upstairs, and Chen Hengcai was in the kitchen. He returned to his hometown the next day. Judge Luo asked Yao, "According to Chen Hengcai's testimony, you held the deceased's hand and Gao stabbed her with force. Is that true?" Yao replied no.

Waiting Outside the Door - Gao Jintang testified that he was from Zhenjiang and worked at a tiger stove on Kangnao Road. He lived not far from Yao Yonggui and was from the same hometown as Chen Hengcai. On that day, Hengcai and Yonggui came and invited him to play. They passed by the Zhang family's door. The two of them went inside, and he waited outside the door. After a while, the two of them came out again and told him to leave quickly. He did not know anything else.

Did Not Return the Deposit Book - Zhang Wenqing testified that she was twenty-four years old. Her father, Zhang Fusheng, had died many years ago. Her mother, Su, was taken by her stepmother last year because she was ill. After her mother recovered, her stepmother refused to return the deposit book. She reported the loss to the bank. There were more than 5,000 taels in Siming Bank and more than 2,000 taels in Xingye Bank. Her stepmother then filed a criminal complaint against her mother, but the case was reconciled later.

Dowry Fee Has Been Paid - Her mother also filed a civil lawsuit, ordering the return of management rights and the deposit book. Later, the two parties reached an agreement and withdrew the case. The condition was to pay 1,500 taels of silver as her dowry and 1,000 taels for her mother's living expenses. But although her expenses had been paid and given to her, her mother's living expenses had not been paid and were still managed by her stepmother.

Borrowed Money to Open a Bookstore - After that, her relationship with her stepmother returned to normal and there were no more opinions. Therefore, she really had no intention of killing her stepmother. At the end of November last year, Chen Hengcai wanted to borrow 1,500 taels of silver from her stepmother to open a bookstore. She interjected, saying that her stepmother should not lend it to him, so she refused. Hengcai held a grudge and wanted to use a pistol against her stepmother.

Stepmother Wanted to Flee - But in October last year, Wang Dabao, the nephew of her stepmother, told her that Su Xiangnian, her stepmother's brother, wanted to harm her because of a lawsuit. In November, she heard Hengcai say that her stepmother wanted to take everything and live elsewhere.

The Small Knife Belongs to Her - She was upstairs when she heard Yao Yonggui talking to her stepmother downstairs. Not long after, she heard an alarm and went downstairs. Yonggui and the others were gone. Her stepmother was lying on the ground with knife wounds. She and a neighboring woman took her to the Red Cross Society for treatment. The small knife used to commit the crime was hers, but it was placed in the drawer of the dressing table and stolen by Hengcai.

Zhang Wenqing Started the Idea - Chen Hengcai testified that the killing of Su was Zhang Wenqing's idea. They had been discussing it for two months. Because of the lawsuit, she asked him to help her and said that she could pay him. She told him to call someone to kill Su, and she agreed to give him 400 yuan, with 50 yuan paid in advance. At 4:45 that afternoon, he gave Gao Jintang 20 yuan in a nearby alley. At that time, he and Yonggui were together. The murder weapon was given to Gao Jintang by Wenqing at this time. The three of them entered Zhang's house together. He did not go with them.

Investigating the Bloody Handprint - Finally, Judge Luo summoned the deceased's younger brother, Su Yaoting, for questioning. After the lawyers for both parties questioned the above people, it was getting late. Judge Luo said that according to Su Yaoting's complaint, there were still bloody handprints on the door of Zhang's house. He then announced that the case would be postponed and instructed the police to investigate whether there were any handprints on the door, and to summon witnesses for continued questioning. After the announcement, the court was adjourned and the defendants were returned to custody.

The Chen Sun Case in Suzhou Will Have Bones Steamed for Examination

Chen Shuangxi, nicknamed Jiangbei the Great King, who opened a teahouse in Suzhou's Changmen, had a son named Chen Xueshi, who married Chen Sun, the daughter of Sun Zhengwen from the Hengshun Cigarette Paper Shop on Laiyuan Bridge in Xumen. In February of last year, Chen Sun suddenly died. The Chen family claimed that she had hanged herself, while the Sun family claimed that she had been strangled to death. They reported it to the Wuxian District Court for examination, which found that she had hanged herself. The court then acquitted her. The Sun family did not accept the verdict and appealed to the High Court and the Supreme Court, but both were rejected. The Sun family still refused to accept the verdict and insisted that she had been strangled to death and requested a transfer of jurisdiction. Now, the higher court has designated the Shanghai District Court to investigate. However, the body should be re-examined. Therefore, the two parties were summoned the day before yesterday, and Prosecutor Yang opened the court for preliminary examination and ordered them to sign a guarantee to transport the coffin to Shanghai for steaming the bones for examination. The two parties have complied with the order and went to Suzhou to transport the body to the District Court. Because the procedure of steaming the bones is very complicated, the General Affairs Office was ordered yesterday to hire workers to build stoves, etc. As soon as the coffin arrives at the court, the steaming examination will be carried out.

Three Robbers Sentenced to Death

Robbers Gu Changchun, Zhou Cailao, Yu Zhongjin, etc., kidnapped Zhu Maosheng's eight-year-old son Desheng, the owner of the Laoda Fang Tea and Food Shop at No. 864 and a half, Mengnala Road, at noon on December 11th of last year. They hid him in a house at No. 79 Shoxiang Lane, Fangbang Road, in the Chinese territory. Later, detective Feng Zhiming and others from the Laozha Police Station cracked the case, and together with Ge Wangshi, the woman guarding the hostage, they were brought to the Provisional Court for investigation and trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Gao Junxiang opened the court and pronounced the verdict: Gu, Zhou, and Yu, the three robbers, were each sentenced to death, and Ge Wangshi was sentenced to life imprisonment. After the judgment, they were ordered to be separately detained, pending submission for approval and execution.

Robbers in the Zheng Ruijuan Kidnapping Case Could Not Be Identified

Zheng Ruijuan, the daughter of Zheng Xitang of Ping An Company, was kidnapped by bandits in front of Yucai School on Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen, and later emerged safely in Xujiahui. After the incident, Han Shentang and Xi Ayue were arrested by the Second Precinct of the First District and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which then transferred them to the Local Court for investigation. After the investigation was completed, a public prosecution was filed. Yesterday, Judge Deng opened the court for trial. The defendants all denied the charges. When questioned by the victim Zheng Ruijuan, it was difficult to identify them. The chauffeur Jiang A'er was also summoned to court. The judge ordered six defendants in another case to be lined up for identification, but Jiang also had difficulty identifying them. Then, patrol officer Song Huanzhong testified that he had arrested the two defendants after receiving a report. The judge repeatedly questioned them for a long time. Finally, after the prosecutor finished his arguments and the lawyer made his defense, the judge declared the debate closed and ordered the defendants to await sentencing. The defendants were returned to custody.

The Appeal of the Dalun Real Estate Eviction Case Opens

Both Sides Unwilling to Concede

Yesterday's Debate Concluded

Dalun Real Estate Company, intending to build a nine-story building after leasing a plot of land at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Fujian Road to Da Zhonghua Department Store, notified seventeen shops, including the Laoda Fang Tea and Food Shop currently operating there, to relocate to facilitate reconstruction. The tenants refused, resulting in a lawsuit. After the preliminary trial in the Provisional Court, the tenants lost the case. Except for two households, the remaining fifteen all refused to accept the verdict and filed an appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Hu, the presiding judge of the Civil Division of the Court of Appeal, along with judges Zhong and Lin, opened the court for a joint hearing. The courtroom was extremely crowded with spectators. First, Judge Hu advised both parties to resolve the matter peacefully to avoid a lengthy lawsuit and inquired about the landlord's willingness to compromise. The lawyer representing Dalun immediately stated that they had originally decided to allow three months of rent so that the defendants could get through the Lunar New Year period. Now, in accordance with the court's intentions, they would again persuade the landlord to extend the grace period by three months. Then, the tenants' claims were heard. According to their lawyer, the buildings were not old and there was no real need for reconstruction. Moreover, the landlord leased the land to Da Zhonghua for an annual rent of 100,000 taels of silver. Now, the tenants were also willing to increase their annual rent from 60,000 taels to 100,000 taels. When the houses were initially rented, the oral agreement was for a term of 20 years. The tenants who had lived there the longest had only been there for eight years. If they were to relocate, regardless of the order of rental, they should all be re-leased for another twelve years. The court also inquired whether the contract with Da Zhonghua stipulated any damages for breach of contract. According to Dalun's lawyer, the contract stipulated that Da Zhonghua would pay an annual ground rent of 100,000 taels of silver, and in addition, compensate Dalun for a portion of the cost of building the house. If the cost was 700,000 to 1,200,000 taels, then Da Zhonghua would have to pay interest of 70,000 to 120,000 taels per year in addition to the ground rent. Even if the contract did not stipulate damages, merchants valued integrity and could not easily breach the contract. Judge Hu also inquired whether the issue of the Hibiya Yoko store's relocation had been resolved. If it had not been resolved, even if the tenants in this case relocated, there would still be shortcomings and a nine-story building could not be constructed. He also lamented that Chinese people raised huge sums of money to start department stores, but mostly sold foreign goods and did not know how to revitalize domestic products. Dalun's lawyer replied that the Hibiya Yoko relocation issue would be negotiated separately after the settlement of this case. The court made all sorts of comparisons, but both sides were unwilling to concede and there was no way to reconcile. They could only proceed with the trial. The hearing continued until dusk and the debate concluded. The court ordered that a date be set for sentencing.

The Wusong Kidnapping Case Cracked

The Hostage Was Escorted Home Yesterday

Two More Bandit Boats Seized

The Main Kidnappers Are Still Under Investigation

Zhou Zou, an elderly woman from Zhoujiaqiao, West of Wusong Town, had her twelve-year-old grandson Quanlin kidnapped for the second time on December 22nd of last year around 6 PM, with a ransom demand of 20,000 yuan. The case had been going on for four months and there had been no news. Unexpectedly, around 2 PM on the 10th, the Zhabei squad leader Wang Shifu, Su Sheng, detectives Wang Yao, etc., of the Public Security Bureau, along with informants, rescued the young hostage Zhou Quanlin from a bungalow at No. 4 London Road, and arrested the kidnappers Li Jinxiu, Liu Chuan Cai, Chen Tongling, etc. Details were reported in the 11th issue of this newspaper. It is now learned that the young hostage Zhou Quanlin had already been escorted from Shanghai to the Public Security Bureau of the Seventh District of Wusong by detectives Su and Wang of the Public Security Bureau yesterday (the 12th) at 1 PM. The bureau notified his mother, Zhou Zhang, to come to the bureau to take him home. When the mother and son suddenly met, they were overwhelmed with joy and grief, and they embraced and wept incessantly, moving all who watched. It is reported that around 9 AM on the 11th, two more bandit boats related to the case were seized near Yinhangpu. One main kidnapper is still under investigation.

Mr. Ao Erqi of the Power Company Will Return Home on Schedule

The Business Community Casts a Golden Tripod as a Gift

Mr. Ao Erqi of the former Public Works Bureau's Electrical Department, now the Shanghai Power Company, has worked in the public electricity industry for twenty-eight years. His deeds and merits are well known throughout Shanghai. It is now learned that he has resigned and retired and is scheduled to return to England this Saturday (the 15th). Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the business community initiated a fundraising campaign to cast a golden tripod as a gift to commemorate his departure. Those listed as donors include Qian Longzhang, Yuan Ludeng, Wu Yunzhai, Li Fusun, Xu Xinzhi, Xu Jiqing, Sun Jingxi, Bei Songsun, Lin Kanghou, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Busun, Xu Qingyun, Xu Tingzuo, Xu Tonghao, Feng Bingnan, and others. A tea party will be held today (the 13th) at 5 PM in the officer's room of the International Business Corps Club on the fourth floor of No. 17 Fuzhou Road to bid him farewell.

Shanghai Working Women's International Banquet

Evening of the 18th

Working women in Shanghai have long lacked a well-organized organization. Although women from various countries in Shanghai have various independent groups, they have very few opportunities to connect with each other. This time, the YWCA expanded its services and solicited opinions from women of all countries in Shanghai regarding the construction of a new clubhouse, which is the starting point for women of all countries in Shanghai to cooperate. Now, the YWCA will hold a grand banquet for all working women in Shanghai at the American Women's Association address at No. 113 Jing'an Temple Road next Tuesday, February 18th, which is a new milestone in the united women's movement in Shanghai.

It is known that working women in various countries around the world, whether in the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, or Japan, all have a grand annual banquet. Shanghai has never had one before. From now on, Shanghai will not be at a disadvantage in this regard. Moreover, uniting all working women, regardless of national boundaries, to gather and enjoy themselves in one place is the starting point for women from different countries to communicate with each other and is in line with the world trend. It is also heard that the banquet next Tuesday will have "national team" organizations to allow representatives of each country to highlight the characteristics of their country, and there will be various performances from various countries. It will definitely be a grand occasion. This event is managed by a joint committee of Chinese, American, British, German, Japanese, Portuguese, and Russian individuals. The cost per person is 1.6 yuan. Those who wish to participate can purchase tickets at the YWCA at No. 4 Museum Road.

The YMCA Holds an Integrity Campaign

Soliciting Signatures Against Dog Racing and Roulette Gambling

The Sichuan Road YMCA will hold a large-scale integrity campaign for three days from the 13th to the 15th of this month to promote virtues such as thrift, diligence, honesty, and savings, in order to cultivate good citizens. The general order is as follows: in addition to the all-day exhibition displaying various pictures and specimens for people to view, famous people will be invited to speak at 5:30 PM every afternoon. The first day will be Mr. Zhao Jinqing's "Integrity Saves the Country," the second day will be Mr. Qian Xinzhi's "The Importance of Savings," and the third day will be Mr. Zhang Zhijiang's "Simple Life." There will be movies and new dramas at 8 PM every night. Admission tickets can be obtained temporarily from the association. Children will not be admitted.

In addition, the Nanshi Puyi Society of the YMCA, the Vocational Education Society of the French Concession, and the Pudong Public Society of Yangshupu, in view of the increasing gambling trend in Shanghai and the severe harm caused by dog racing and roulette gambling, intend to take advantage of the integrity campaign to send letters to the authorities of the British and French Concessions, requesting that they be investigated and banned immediately. The draft of the letter is as follows: "Respectfully, in order to seek social peace and tranquility, it is necessary to eliminate local evils first. The gambling trend in Shanghai has always been rampant. Since the existence of dog racing venues and roulette gambling dens, gamblers in general have become more blatant, and the huge sums of money won and lost day and night are shocking. Young men and women who are addicted to it, losing their fortunes and their personalities, are frequently heard of. Such harm to the community and disaster to society, if not strictly prohibited, would be a disservice to the citizens. Maintaining humanity and rectifying morality are the responsibilities of your bureau. Therefore, in the public interest of the people, we hereby submit this letter to your bureau for review and request that you promptly order the investigation and closure of all dog racing venues and roulette gambling dens within the concession, to eliminate harm to the local area and to show public concern. Those interested in expressing their sympathy from all walks of life can sign their names at the above locations and submit a letter of petition to reverse the declining trend."

The China Children's Welfare Association Emphasizes Vocational Education for Disaster-Stricken Children

Chairman Jiang issued instructions to the China Children's Welfare Association, saying, "Today, the ability to educate children lies not only in strengthening their bodies and cultivating their morals, but also in developing their vocational skills for independent livelihood. There are many vagrants in our country today. The reason for this is that most of them did not acquire a vocational skill in their childhood. By the time they reach adulthood, they are unable to farm, unable to do business, and unable to work as laborers. Looking after themselves, they are completely unable to do anything. As a result of their inability to make a living, they are led astray, which is very pitiful. I hope that your association will promote children's vocations and teach them skills so that they can become independent people." Therefore, the association attaches particular importance to children's vocational education and plans to select ten disaster-stricken children to go to the Xiangshan Children's Welfare Institute in Beiping to learn crafts in order to implement vocational education. It is now learned that the association has selected ten disaster-stricken children who are being fostered in orphanages in Shanghai, who are strong and intelligent, and escorted them to the port yesterday morning at 8 AM by Zhang Junkang, the director of the Longhua Shanghai Orphanage, Mr. Wu Weide, the general secretary of the association, and Mr. Zhang Yueru, the executive secretary, and took the Tangshan Maru to Tianjin, where they transferred to a train to Peiping. It is said that the disaster-stricken children were taken in by the Children's Welfare Association from disaster areas such as Canggou, Teng County, Shandong Province, and have been fostered in orphanages in Shanghai for more than a year. In addition to reading and writing, they also practice woodworking, rattan work, bamboo work, tailoring, and other crafts, working half-time and studying half-time, with considerable success. The association heard that the crafts of the Xiangshan Children's Welfare Institute are well-organized, so they specially selected ten people to go to study, in order to alleviate the burden of teaching and raising in the Shanghai Orphanage. When in port, Wu, the general secretary of the Children's Welfare Association, delivered a farewell speech, saying, "You have been in Shanghai for more than a year and have been taught and raised by the Shanghai Orphanage, and you have a basic foundation in knowledge. Our association is planning for your future independence and is sending you to the Xiangshan Children's Welfare Institute in Beiping to learn crafts. We hope that you will work hard and make progress, so as not to let down the good intentions of the association, and to make capital for your future lives. He also said, "You all come from disaster areas and are like brothers in adversity. You should love each other and take care of each other on the way, so that you can go to the Ping Institute safely." It is heard that the ship tickets for the disaster-stricken children were subsidized by Wang Yiting, a famous philanthropist in Shanghai, and that China Travel Service specially sent personnel to Tianjin and Peiping to provide free transportation.

The Bāxiānqiáo Vegetable Market Relocates for Business

The Bāxiānqiáo vegetable market in the French Concession has been around for a long time, so the French Public Works Bureau plans to rebuild it into a cement and steel-framed vegetable market to last a long time. It has hired workers to build a simple shed on the open space opposite the Sino-French School on Mintiniyin Road, in preparation for the relocation of the Bāxiānqiáo vegetable market while it is being demolished and rebuilt, so as not to affect business. The electricity has now been installed in the shed. The French Public Works Bureau has also sent personnel to place shelves horizontally in the shed and assign numbers from No. 1 to No. 300 to avoid disputes. Powder lines have also been drawn on the ground to limit the stalls, which must be set up within the powder line boundaries, otherwise they will be fined. According to the vegetable vendors, the French Public Works Bureau has scheduled to build a fence and demolish the Bāxiānqiáo vegetable market on the 17th of this month, so all the stalls will be moved to the shed at the same time. Once the new building of the Bāxiānqiáo vegetable market is completed, they will have to move back.

Pitiable Woman Marries Her Lover

Dài Rúzhēn Seeks Freedom After Losing It

Dài Rúzhēn, a woman from Dōngtái, is 21 years old and exceptionally beautiful. Her father, Xiānglín, is a carpenter, and her mother, Wén, is getting older. She was quite favored by her parents when she was young. When she was 17 years old, her father, due to economic difficulties, sold his daughter to a brothel run by Lǐ Bǐng in Rúgāo, receiving 80 silver dollars as her body price. After entering the world of prostitution, Rúzhēn severed ties with her parents. She engaged in the trade of flesh and blood, and her charm attracted many patrons, making her very busy. However, the authorities have recently been strictly banning prostitution, and Lǐ Bǐng has found it difficult to maintain his business. He soon closed down and wanted to resell Rúzhēn. However, Rúzhēn met a clerk named Gù Lánbō in the local Public Security Bureau last year. They fell deeply in love and sowed the seeds of affection. Rúzhēn took the opportunity to elope with Gù and made a golden house in a certain alley in the area. Unexpectedly, their secret was discovered by Lǐ, who went to negotiate. Gù took Rúzhēn to live elsewhere, and Lǐ knew about it but pretended not to hear it. However, Gù wanted to solve the problem once and for all. A week ago, he led Rúzhēn to Shanghai and stayed in a small South Gate inn, living together like husband and wife. Unexpectedly, Rúzhēn's father suddenly missed his daughter and went to Lǐ's place to inquire. He learned that his daughter had eloped with her lover. He suddenly came up with an idea and wanted to take Lǐ to the local Public Security Bureau, ordering Lǐ to hand over his daughter within a time limit. Lǐ was extremely anxious and immediately ordered his friend Hé Sān to take a car to Shanghai to search for her. Yesterday, while passing by the Qiújiāng Road area, he caught sight of Rúzhēn and Gù riding in a rickshaw. He immediately called the local police and arrested them in the Second Precinct of the Fifth District. During the preliminary interrogation by Director Táo, Rúzhēn firmly refused to return to her hometown with Hé and was willing to grow old with Gù. As the case involved enticing her to run away, it was handed over to the judicial section for verification.

Lǐ Zhàobǐng's Home Robbery Case Involved His Nephew

Detained for Requesting Photos

Two More Robbers Arrested

Lǐ Zhàobǐng, a Guangdong native, lives at No. 2017 North Sìchuān Road. On the afternoon of the 7th of this month, four robbers broke into his home and stole property worth 1,433 silver dollars. After the incident, Lǐ reported the case to the police station in charge and requested an investigation. The Chinese and foreign detectives rushed to Lǐ's house to investigate and found a photo. According to the victim, it was a portrait of his nephew Lǐ Zhàoquán. Zhàoquán used to work for him but resigned three years ago and had been wandering around. The detective took the photo back to the police station for investigation. On the 10th, Zhàoquán suddenly went to his uncle's house to ask for the photo, but he did not meet Zhàobǐng. Therefore, he went again the day before yesterday and was arrested by the police. He was considered a suspect in the robbery case. Yesterday morning, Judge Tán Xīnzhèn brought him to the Provisional Court for interrogation. Lǐ Zhàobǐng described the robbery. According to Lǐ Zhàoquán, after being dismissed by his uncle, he lived in a certain labor union and worked as a substitute worker. He went to the Guǎngzhēn Building on Fourth Horse Road every day. He heard that his uncle's house had been robbed, so he went to his uncle's place and learned that his photo had been taken away by the police. Therefore, he went to ask for it the day before yesterday and was arrested. The police station stated that the case was still under investigation and requested a postponement. They also said that after the defendant was arrested, they arrested two robbers involved in the case at No. 26 Qiújiāng Road. Because the area belonged to the Chinese territory, the two robbers were detained in the Public Security Bureau and requested that a document be sent to transfer them. Judge Tán ordered Lǐ Zhàoquán to be detained, pending a letter to the Public Security Bureau to transfer the robbers to the case for further interrogation.

Accused of Selling Counterfeit Banknotes

Zhōu Fùchāng, also known as Wáng Liánshēng, from Ānhuī, colluded with those who manufactured counterfeit banknotes, sold fake tickets, and disrupted the financial system. The Hóngkǒu police station learned of this and ordered detectives to purchase them the day before yesterday. The asking price was 25 yuan per 100 yuan. They purchased 20 fake tickets worth 5 yuan each and arrested Zhōu. The bank also identified them as counterfeit. Afterward, detectives went to Zhōu's residence at No. 1253 Wúsōng Road to search and found 11 fake tickets in an envelope, including 1 yuan and 5 yuan denominations. According to Zhōu, the fake tickets were given to him by Chén Ābǎo in the General Chamber of Commerce on Fourth Horse Road. Chinese and foreign detectives went to investigate and learned that it was Zhōu's false accusation. Zhōu used to work in the General Chamber of Commerce but was punished by the government for stealing items reported by Chén and Fā. Therefore, he wanted to use his old grudges to falsely accuse them. Yesterday morning, Zhōu and the counterfeit banknotes were sent to the Provisional Court. Judge Tán Xīnzhèn brought him to trial. The Chinese and foreign detectives detailed the course of the case and requested a postponement, fearing that the defendant might have committed other cases, so that they could start an investigation. Judge Tán granted the request and ordered the defendant to be detained for further questioning at a later date.

Robbers Arrested for Night Walking

At 3 AM yesterday morning, four strong men passed by Xīnjiān Road and were seen by two Chinese patrol officers at No. 2351 and No. 2631, who considered them suspicious for wandering around in the middle of the night. They were searched, but nothing was found at first, so they were released. Unexpectedly, they were indeed bandits. When the patrol officers searched them, they took advantage of the dark night to throw away two sharp knives they were carrying. The patrol officers saw the knives on the ground after the four bandits left and immediately chased them, but only three bandits were caught and brought to the Xīnzha Gate Police Station. They confessed their names as Sū Bǎo Hé, Lǔ Āxiáng, and Zhū Xiángshēng. The three bandits also admitted that at 3 AM the day before yesterday, they and Xiàng Āgēn and others robbed Zhào Yúnqīng of a coat and 12 silver dollars at Pàikè Road Jiàngyuán Lane. Xiàng was hiding at No. 173 Tōngshāng Inn on Àiwényì Road. The chief ordered Sergeant Gāo Yànróng to arrest Xiàng. They were sent to the Provisional Court for questioning yesterday. However, Zhào's address was unknown and he could not be summoned. Judge Luó interrogated them once and ordered the defendants to be returned to custody for further questioning at a later date.

Nameless Male Corpse with Shattered Head and Severed Wrist

A New Ghost on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway

A man was crushed to death by a train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway track west of Jìng'ān Temple Sānjīng Temple in the west of Shanghai the night before last. The local guarantor Jīn Yúnzhōu reported the case to the Local Court yesterday. Prosecutor Lí and others arrived at the scene and found that the corpse was about 40 years old and looked like a worker. Half of his head was crushed and his wrist was also crushed off, making it a gruesome sight. Photos were taken and the body was taken to the hall for burial.

Rickshaw Puller Knocked Down by a Car

One Dead, One Injured

Jiǎ Fāyǒu, a 44-year-old rickshaw puller from Jiangbei, living at No. 78, Lane 86, Avenue de Mèrsine, French Concession, went out with his companion, Mr. A, to work early in the morning on the 11th. While passing the intersection of Avenue de Mèrsine and Avenue Joffre, a car No. 373 driven by Jīn Gēnxiáng, the driver of a mansion at No. 795 Mǎitè Hèsītū Road in the Public Concession, came along. Jiǎ and Mr. A were unable to avoid it and were both knocked down and injured. Patrol officer No. 588 arrived and took the injured person and Jīn to the police station. The chief ordered the injured person to be sent to the Guangci Hospital for treatment and Jīn to be released on bail. Jīn had no bail bond. However, Jiǎ died at 8 PM that day due to a severe head injury. The hospital notified the police station and the body was taken to the Tóngrén Fúyuán Hall corpse inspection station. Yesterday, the police station ordered detectives to inform the relatives of the deceased, Yáng Dà (the deceased's cousin), to come to the station. Zhū, the presiding judge of the French Public Court, was informed by the Vehicle Department and arrived at the station at 3 PM to inspect the corpse. He took his seat and heard the report from the chief of the Vehicle Department, as well as the defendant, witnesses, and relatives of the deceased. After questioning them about the circumstances of the collision, he declared that the deceased died from injuries sustained from being hit by a car. He allowed the relatives to prepare a coffin and collect the body, and he would wait for the court to investigate. It is heard that Mr. A is still being treated in the hospital, and Jīn's driving license is only half-certified as he is still in training.

Autopsy of a Deceased Kidnapper

The Public Concession's Public Works Bureau Hospital reported the death of a prisoner the day before yesterday. In accordance with the regulations, the West Prison police chief notified the Huìsī Police Station, which had handled the case. The police sent the body to the Fèilún Road corpse inspection station and reported it to the Provisional Court. Judge Gě Sìxūn was commissioned to inspect the body at 11 AM yesterday. He took his seat and heard the complaint from the Western deputy police chief of the Huìsī Police Station that the deceased, Gōng Āqìng, was sentenced to life imprisonment in the kidnapping case on August 21, 1929, after a trial in the court. He was in good health when he first entered prison, but later suffered from lung disease and was sent to the Public Works Bureau Hospital for treatment on February 6, 1930. He died on the afternoon of the 11th, and it was found that he had no family. Judge Gě, having heard the report and finding that the deceased had died of illness and had no family, ordered that Shànshān Villa be代為棺殮.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Arrests Many Robbers

The Municipal Public Security Bureau's Detective Squad received a tip-off yesterday morning that Zhāng Hànqīng from Jiāngdū, a gang leader who specializes in street robbery, was hiding in a house at No. 15 Wànxīng Lane, Hànzhōng Road, in the Fourth District of Zháběi, and requested that personnel be dispatched to arrest him quickly. Captain Qiáo, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered the Zhabei squad leader Sū Shēng, Wáng Shìfú, detectives Yīn Xīngchūn, Wáng Yào, Dòu Yùlín, Yìng Hǎifā, Huáng Jìngsān, and others to go to the address and arrest Zhāng in the house on the spot. They also seized a four-inch fake pistol, a flashlight, a leather box, 20 silver dollars, a gold ring, two pawn tickets, and a gold-plated watch. They interrogated him on the spot. He confessed that he was 25 years old, named Xiǎo Wāng Zi, and worked as a leather craftsman. He also confessed that he had repeatedly gathered crowds to rob pedestrians in various places such as Lùjiāzhuāng and Mǎnzhōu Road, and had stolen fur robes, gold jewelry, gold watches, and cash, which he pawned. He had committed eight crimes in less than two months this year. At the same time, he also confessed the whereabouts of his accomplices. Captain Qiáo again ordered the original officers to arrest four men and women in different places and interrogate them on the spot. One confessed that his name was Wáng Dàmáo, 22 years old, from Fùníng, and lived at No. 12 of 25 Jiān, Lùjiāzhuāng, Zháběi. One confessed that his name was Hán Xiǎo Qīzi, 19 years old, from Fùníng, and pulled a rickshaw for a living in the thatched sheds of the Tàiyáng Temple in Zháběi. One confessed that his name was Yú Xiǎoyǒuzi, 32 years old, from Jiāngdū, and lived in a flat in Xiàjiā Lane, Zháběi. A woman confessed that her name was Wáng Àibǎo, 17 years old, from the local area, and lived at No. 11 Sāndé Lane, Yáojiā Stone Bridge, Zháběi. She had only met Wáng Dàmáo on the 5th of this month, so she did not know that Wáng had committed a crime. The others all admitted that they had repeatedly committed robbery with Zhāng in the Róngshēng Lane, Lùjiāzhuāng, Mǎnzhōu Road, and Wūzhèn Road in Zháběi, and had used the stolen goods for pawning. After Captain Qiáo interrogated them, he immediately prepared a document and sent them to the Third Section for questioning.

Ke Shenyuan's Imprisonment Reduced to Three Years

Ke Thanks the Court and Lawyers

Ke Shenyuan, a native of Ningbo, established the Jinsheng Trading Company on Ningbo Road in the British Concession last October. He used bad checks to defraud six households, including Tu Cexun, of goods worth several thousand silver dollars. Tu and others reported him, and the Provisional Court sentenced him to six counts of fraud, each with two years of imprisonment, for a total of six years, and ordered him to compensate the plaintiffs. Ke was not satisfied and hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to appeal. The Court of Appeal held a hearing, and lawyer Shen presented various reasons and debated with the opposing party. Yesterday afternoon, presiding Judge Qiu and associate judges Shen and Li announced the verdict, revoking the original sentence and reducing Ke Shenyuan's imprisonment to three years. Upon hearing the verdict, Ke thanked the court and lawyer Shen, and was then taken away by the police for execution of the sentence.

Washing Feet in a Washbasin

Leads to a Broken Skull

Jiang Liyuan, a 32-year-old man from Shandong, worked as a laborer at the Rihua Yarn Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong. After finishing work at around 6 PM the night before, he went to the factory's washroom to wash his hands and face as usual. At that time, many people were crowding and jostling, all trying to get ahead. Unexpectedly, Jin Dajun, a fellow worker from Gaoyou, placed both feet in the washbasin to wash them. Jiang was very angry and confronted Jin. Jin, embarrassed, went outside to gather several people to wait at the factory gate. When Jiang passed by, they confronted him, and an argument led to a violent scuffle. Jiang, unprepared, was struck on the head with an iron bar by Jin, causing him to bleed profusely. A police patrol from the Fourth Division happened to pass by and arrested Jin Dajun, along with the injured Jiang Liyuan, and took them to the Third District Public Security Bureau. The district chief, considering the case involved assault, transferred them to the District Court yesterday.

Russian Red Cross Launches Baby Foster Care Program

Wenhui Bao reports that the Russian Red Cross at 876 Avenue Joffre has recently launched a baby foster care program to organize baby nurseries. Working women can send their young children to the nursery in the morning and pick them up after work in the evening. The nursery will hire married women, experienced nannies, and doctors to take care of the children. Initially, a fee will be charged, but once sufficient funds are available, the nursery plans to provide free care and food.

Over Twenty Gamblers Punished

Inspector Zhang of the First Precinct, First Division in the South City discovered suspicious gambling activities in the home of Ni Agou at 1 Nanjing Street. The place was crowded with various types of people, posing a significant threat to local security. At around 9 PM the night before, he led patrol officer Jin Xiliang and others to secretly raid the house. They apprehended more than twenty gamblers, including Wang Shouchang, Lu Changsheng, Wu Asan, Gu Baobao, Hou Baobao, Yuan Yongcheng, Zhang Jinming, Guo Fugen, Yang Maomao, Chen Xihe, Jiang Liansheng, Jiang Shikun, Peng Qingbao, Zhu Abao, Wu Agen, Xia Jinshou, Wang Agen, Zhang Genrong, Zhou Agen, and Qu Agen from Yangzhou, Wu Changgen from Shaoxing, and others. They were taken back to the station along with gambling paraphernalia, gambling money, and Ni's wife, Zhang. After preliminary interrogation by the station chief, they were ordered to be punished according to the law as a warning. The gambling paraphernalia was destroyed.

Embezzlement of Funds Leads to Three Months Imprisonment

Each Given a Two-Year Reprieve

Yao Cuosun and Fei Xixi, employees of the Continental Bank on Beijing Road, were accused of embezzling 8,000 taels of the bank's funds. They were interrogated by the Provisional Court and ordered to post 5,000 yuan bail each. Since they could not provide bail, they were detained in the police station. Yesterday morning, the date for the verdict arrived, and the defendants' lawyers, including Zhu Sifu, appeared in court. Judge Gao announced the verdict, sentencing each defendant to three months of imprisonment with a two-year reprieve. The private lawsuit will be filed with the Civil Court by the plaintiff.

Bandits Rob Pedestrian Under Threat of Force

Bandit Zhou Ayu, together with the fugitive Lu Afu, stopped pedestrian Lu Lizhao near the Gu'en Temple on Avenue Villemon in the French Concession late last month. They brandished a pistol and threatened him, robbing him of a woolen overcoat and several silver dollars before fleeing. Detectives and inspectors of the French Police, including Jin Jiulin, Wang Rusong, and Zhang Daorong, apprehended Zhou and his accomplice, Rong Gengsheng, and found a pistol on Zhou's person. They recovered the stolen goods and brought them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought before the French Concession Court for investigation. The plaintiff testified about the robbery, and Zhou Ayu confessed that Lu Afu, who was still at large, had initiated the robbery and invited him to participate. Rong Gengsheng claimed he was not present at the scene and only received one dollar from Lu Afu afterward, unaware of the robbery, and pleaded for leniency. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhou to five years in the Western Prison and Rong to one month, after which both would be permanently deported. The pistol was confiscated, and the stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Robbers Each Imprisoned for Five Years

Robbers Wang Baolin and Ni Wengui conspired to rob a cigarette and paper store at 603 Avenue Blane-Montmairan in the New French Concession. The shop employees blew the whistle, and French police detectives, including Qian Yumin, arrived and apprehended Wang and Ni. They found a knife and a tattered incense stick, used to imitate a pistol, on their persons, along with the stolen money. They were taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought before the French Concession Court for investigation. Plaintiff Lin Baohua testified about the robbery, and Wang Baolin and Ni Wengui were each sentenced to five years in the Western Prison, after which they would be permanently expelled from the concession.

Xu Heling, the Shanghai District Court prosecutor, was recently appointed by the Jiangsu High Court as the chief prosecutor of the newly established Wuxi County Court. After accepting the appointment, Mr. Xu has already handed over his old duties and gone to Suzhou to thank the High Court for the appointment and take up his new post.

Four-Five-Six Refurbished and Reopened

The Four-Five-Six Food Company on Nanjing Road, east of Pintang Lane, has long been renowned in Shanghai for its Yangzhou dim sum and Sichuan cuisine. Although there have been internal improvements over the past three years, the facilities have never been renovated. Recognizing this, the company closed for business in late December of the old calendar to completely refurbish. The dim sum section has hired famous chefs from Yangzhou, and the Sichuan cuisine section has been completely reorganized, focusing on taste and not just appearance. Western pastries, coffee, black tea, and green tea have also been added to help customers sit and chat. It is said that all prices have been reduced. The third floor has a special room, elegantly decorated, that can accommodate three full tables, making it especially suitable for group dinners in Shanghai.

Cheng Lin, the chief of the First Sub-Bureau of the County Public Bureau in Minhang Town, was dismissed for ineffective enforcement of the opium ban. The County Public Security Bureau Chief Zhu reported this to the County Government, which dismissed Cheng. Xu Baiyi has been appointed to act as the chief of the sub-bureau.

The Pan-Pacific Association of this port will host a dinner on the 21st of this month, inviting the renowned international political scholar Dr. Ji Feng, and asking him to give a speech on the countries along the Pacific coast of South America. Shanghai South Tobacco Industry Announces a General Meeting

The Shanghai South Tobacco Industry Association, in order to reorganize its affairs and promote national goods, had originally scheduled a general meeting for yesterday. However, due to incomplete procedures, it has been postponed to the 18th. Yesterday, the association notified its members, stating that member Nan Yongtai and other tobacco shops near the Dadongmen wrote that their Chinese domestic tobacco businesses have been severely impacted by the influx of foreign cigarettes. People prioritize convenience over patriotism, resulting in a massive outflow of money. The lack of unity hinders efforts to remedy the situation. The tobacco shops, being weak, have switched to selling tobacco and sundries. Fortunately, the association has advised them in writing, and the newspapers have encouraged and supported them, helping them stand their ground (omitted section). The influence of the financial crisis has affected all industries, and the tax reform based on gold units has led to a sharp increase in the price of goods. Retail prices have decreased. Maintaining the old sales prices would result in significant losses. The association, together with the other eight member associations, should have senior members participate in the introductions, uniting together to prevent divisions among the members. Future elected officials should also fulfill their obligations and actively proceed. A general meeting will be held at 1 PM on February 18th at the Tobacco Industry Association in Dong Yaojia Lane to thoroughly reorganize business rules, exchange foreign currencies, display price tags, and set uniform prices, as well as discuss the association's fee collection plan. It is crucial that the managing directors of the precious companies attend on time and make decisions. This is hereby notified.

Great Eastern Stocking Factory to Move to New Location

The Great Eastern Stocking Factory on Nanjing Road has been in business for six years. Under the leadership of Mr. Geng, the business has been very prosperous. The Bee brand products are durable and practical. Due to the impending renovation of the original location, the factory is moving to the former site of the Sun Company, across from the Rainbow Temple on the same road. New-style storefronts are being constructed, and it is expected that the move will be completed by the end of next month.

The New Asia Chemical Pharmaceutical Co., Ltd. at 24 White Rock Road sells various products, including cosmetics such as Peacock brand tooth powder, toothpaste, Peacock cream, hair tonic, and perfume essence, as well as Western medicines. The company has hired Western medical experts to research and produce over a hundred kinds of products. Recently, major pharmacies have been placing orders in large numbers.

Meeting Minutes of the Fresh Medicine Industry Association

The Fresh Medicine Industry Association held a general meeting yesterday, with Secretary Wang Lixian as chairman. The agenda was as follows: 1) Discussion of the Chamber of Commerce's letter urging payment of regular fees. The association's income is limited. It was decided to request the Chamber of Commerce to change the payment method to two installments. Resolution: Passed. 2) Proposal to increase the price of fresh medicine reed stems. It was unanimously agreed that production has been decreasing, resources are becoming scarce, and labor costs have increased, making the original price of 300 cash per catty unprofitable and unsustainable. It was proposed to increase the price to 480 cash to maintain the industry. Resolution: Passed. The secretariat was instructed to send an official letter to the Medicine Industry Association and all pharmacies informing them that the new price will be implemented from February 13th of the Gregorian calendar. Remaining items omitted. Meeting adjourned.

The China Critic Weekly, Volume 3, Issue 7 Published

The China Critic Weekly, Volume 3, Issue 7, was published today. Key articles include: Editorials on "The End of the May Thirtieth Incident," "Shanghai's Various Organizations Welcome Students Studying Abroad," "Speculation and Gambling," and "Proposal to Establish a Mental Hospital in Wuchang." Special articles include Chen Shifu's "Strange Phenomena in Chinese University Education," Wu Zelin's "Psychological View of Foreigners' Hegemonic Behavior," Zhao Minheng's "Plan for Opening Huludao Port," and Wang Yingxi's "Remedies for the Sharp Decline in Silver Prices." Other features include "A Week's Major Events," "Domestic and Foreign Commentary," "New Book Reviews," "Official Documents," and "Various Statistics."

Police Seeking to Identify a Female Corpse

The following female corpse was found in the Huangpu River near the Yangshupu Shipyard at 10 AM on February 9, 1930. She is approximately 25 years old, about 4 feet 8 inches tall, medium build, with black and yellow hair, brown skin, straight nose, pointed chin, low forehead, and ears that protrude forward. She has one gold tooth in her upper jaw. She is wearing black trousers, a black vest, a green crepe jacket, patterned socks, and blue and white waistbands. Anyone who recognizes her is asked to report to the nearest police station.

Lost Boy Awaiting Claim

The City Public Security Bureau reported yesterday that a lost boy, Meng Yechaosheng, was found on Zhaojiabang Road and brought to the First Precinct, Second Division. According to his account, he is seven years old, from Sanbei, Ningbo. His father, elder brother, and sister-in-law run a butcher shop in the city of Shanghai. The shop assistant is named A Shun. Including himself, there are five people. The shop is next to the Dahua Stocking Factory on one side and a confectionery store on the other. He does not know the names of his parents or the detailed address of the shop. The boy was wearing a duckbill cap, a plaid cotton long gown, a willow-cloth cotton robe, a pink flannel shirt, plaid cotton pants, bright red flannel socks, and floral cotton rabbit-head shoes. The boy has been transferred to the Xin Pu Yu Tang orphanage to be cared for while awaiting claim.

Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Reorganization News

Due to the drop in dyeing prices, which has affected labor and management, the three groups of labor, management, and capital in the local silk and satin dyeing industry have been cooperating since last year to reorganize dyeing prices. According to statistics from the end of the old calendar year, the city's closed businesses received tens of thousands of yuan in revenue. For outstanding payments from various silk shops from last year, they prepare to seek legal remedies. Through successive discussions among the managers of various factories in the city, it was decided to implement business equality in order to eliminate the malpractice of greedy dyeing and price reduction. After three rounds of deliberation, the average law ten, nine items were passed, and after all factory managers signed and sealed the agreement, it was submitted to the Dyeing Price Reorganization Committee for public implementation. Regarding the dyeing date of this year, it is stipulated that clothing sections will begin on February 18th. More than ten companies, including Zhenghe, Yi Da, Qian Da, Zhengli, Huacheng, Taisheng, Chengda Long, and Yi Da, have been designated to dye and supply goods. The dyeing date for the source of goods has not yet been determined. However, it is expected that this year, the dye price for the silk shops is in line with the pricing, and there will be no discount. This year, a five-yuan single factory has been designated for dyeing.

Effective Medicine for Frostbite Ulceration

The "Pearl White Jade Cream" invented by Zhengwei Pharmacy (Nanjing Road, west of Wing On Company) is very effective in treating all kinds of skin abrasions. It is especially effective for frostbite ulceration. Once applied to the affected area, it can immediately relieve pain and itching, promote tissue regeneration, and heal the wound. The price is very affordable, only four corners per box, so there is a great demand.

Recent News from Shanghai Civilian Hospital

The Xin Mi Road Civilian Hospital was founded by Chu Minyi, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, and others. The hospital's medical services are provided by doctors Diao Xinde, Kong Xipeng, Xie Qigang, Lin Jiongdong, Gu Sikang, and others, who are in charge of various departments. A French pediatric specialist, Hong Meiying, has been newly hired to specialize in pediatrics. It is reported that the new directors of the hospital include Song Ziwen, Jiao Yitang, Gu Yingfen, Zheng Yuxiu, and Guan Jiong, and they plan to send someone with Hu Wenhu's nephew, Zhongying, to Nanyang to raise funds for the hospital in the near future.

Public Utilities Bureau and General Electric Renew Lamp Contract

Since the Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau took over the management of street lights in Shanghai South, Shanghai North, and various special districts, the lamps used last year were purchased from the General Electric Edison Appliance Company. After one year, the Public Utilities Bureau believes that the quality of the lamps is excellent, bright, and durable, and they are very satisfied. After careful examination by Director Huang Boqiao and Section Chief Zheng Baocheng, they have renewed the contract with Deputy Manager Chuan Yaocheng of the General Electric Edison Appliance Company's Sales Department on February 11th to continue supplying street lights for the entire year.

Hongzhang Silk and Satin Bureau Seeks Name for "Ling"

The Hongzhang Silk and Satin Bureau in Xiaodongmen has a tall and large store with a very exquisite interior, making it a leader in the silk industry in the South City. Since its opening last year, its business has been growing day by day. The newly opened foreign goods department has a complete collection of Western goods and has recently invented a new type of "Ling," which is made of pure silk and is specially designed for women's spring clothing. They are now seeking a name for it. If an elegant and noble name is submitted and selected, the bureau will reward the submitter with a gift.

Rotary Club Annual Banquet Tomorrow Night

The Shanghai Rotary Club will hold its annual banquet and dance party at the Hua Da Hotel at 8 PM on the 14th. All members are encouraged to invite guests to attend. The regular Thursday meal this week will be temporarily canceled.

Robbery Cases in Brief

Dong Tangjia Lane: Around 1 PM yesterday afternoon, four robbers broke into number 601 Dong Tangjia Lane. Three of them were armed with pistols and robbed 473 silver dollars. The victim called the police, who apprehended one robber.

Fujian Road: Around 3:30 AM yesterday morning, someone was robbed by three bandits at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Fujian Road. The victim called the police, and all three bandits were arrested.

News from Various Labor Unions

Dock Workers' Union: The Reorganization Committee held its 20th regular meeting yesterday afternoon. Chairman Wu Jiaze presided over the meeting. The following proposals were discussed: 1) Cao Yizhi proposed that since the union's Second District Union has been officially established, the allowances for the cadres assigned to work in the district, including food and transportation expenses, should be terminated to save money. Decision: Approved, and the accounting department was informed to stop issuing the allowances from February 1st. 2) Chen Haiqiu proposed the resignation of Wu Yunwang, assistant cadre of the document department. Decision: Approved. Hong Boye was appointed to fill the vacancy. 3) Cao Yizhi proposed that the Third Branch of the Fifth District reported that the Fuxin No. 2 Factory dismissed more than 40 packing workers during the Lunar New Year without any reason. The branch repeatedly negotiated with the factory without success and requested assistance. How should this be handled? Decision: The union cadre Duan Xian was instructed to investigate and then review the matter. 4) Wang Shunsheng and Gu Mingsheng, laborers from Yinxiang Port, requested registration and the establishment of a temporary registration office. Decision: Wang Shunsheng was summoned to the meeting for discussion, and the matter will be reviewed. 5) Wu Jiaze proposed that the union is experiencing extreme financial difficulties, and some docks have not paid their monthly fees. The collection cadre, Gu Neiyan, should be instructed to collect the arrears quickly, clearing the arrears within a week. If any docks still have arrears, the cadre should report the facts, and the Reorganization Committee will send a strict letter urging payment. Decision: Passed.

New New Company Employees' Union: The Executive Committee held an emergency meeting the other day and unanimously decided to convene an emergency representative meeting. The situation of the representative meeting is recorded as follows: 1) (Omitted). 2) The company's implementation of Sunday work has become a fact and cannot be canceled. The deadline should be shortened to three months as a trial run. Decision: Passed. A letter will be submitted to the party and government authorities for approval in the name of the representative meeting. 3) Cancellation of the employment contract. Decision: Passed. 4) The company dismissed 39 workers at the end of the year. The Executive Committee has made every effort to negotiate their reinstatement. Decision: Passed. 5) The six workers who were dismissed from the garden department are still requesting the Social Bureau to allow their reinstatement. Decision: Passed. 6) Assistance to Feng Yiyun for reinstatement. Decision: Passed. 7) (Omitted) Temporary motions omitted.

Lithographic Printing Workers' Union: The Executive Committee held a meeting yesterday. Chairman Zhou Yongfa presided over the meeting. The following resolutions were passed: 1) The fourth re-election meeting will be held on March 22nd. 2) Yuan Chang and Fei Zhang Printing Bureaus did not issue New Year's Day wages to the workers. A report will be submitted to the higher authorities for handling. 3) The Printing Industry Association will be requested to notify the bureaus to issue wages on the 14th of the Gregorian calendar and at the end of the month. The 1st and 15th of each month will be rest days for the workers. 4) The placement of unemployed workers will be determined on March 1st.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather in the Yangtze River basin and along the coast is uncertain with possible rain. Shandong is sunny. The wind direction in this area and over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea is unstable. Yesterday's temperature range in this port for the 24 hours prior to 3 PM was a high of 45.8 and a low of 23.0. On the same day last year, the high was 42.6 and the low was 23.5.

Shanghai Local Court

▲ Notice: For the third price reduction auction of the case involving creditor Dong Lantian and debtor Zhou Genglin, etc., due to a loan dispute, this court has sealed and put up for auction the debtor's real estate as listed below. Since the deadline has passed and no one has purchased it, in accordance with the previous price, a reduction of five percent will be made as the lowest price. It is now set for February 26th at this court with the establishment of Box No. 1 for bidding, and bidding will open on March 4th. Residents who wish to purchase the aforementioned real estate must submit their name, age, place of origin, address, and occupation, along with the amount they are willing to offer, in a sealed letter and deposit it in the bid box before the deadline. Bids will be opened according to the law, and the bidder with the highest price will be the successful bidder. The successful bidder must pay one-fifth of the bid price as a deposit on the same day, and the remaining balance must be paid in full upon delivery of the property. This court will then issue a management certificate. If the payment is not made by the deadline, the bidder with the next highest price will be selected and the aforementioned procedure will be followed. All residents are hereby notified, and all interested parties must be present on the day of the bid opening and must not delay. Special notice is hereby given. Details are as follows: (1) Subject of auction: Zhou Jinhua's household registration, 5 minutes, 2 cents, 7 haos.
